  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;

  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;
  }
  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */

  textarea, select, input {

  }
  /* Note: decoupling heading levels from styles is useful for

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





Chromium devtools can be crashed consistently by simply running the very few JS lines in this PoC. 



<span class="line"><!---->Chromium devtools can be crashed consistently by simply running the very few JS lines in this PoC. <!----></span>



<br>





As long as the devtools are closed, the website will function completely normally, but when it's open(/being opened) it will crash along with the website tab itself immediately and consistently.



<span class="line"><!---->As long as the devtools are closed, the website will function completely normally, but when it's open(/being opened) it will crash along with the website tab itself immediately and consistently.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I consider this a security issue because this allows attackers detect and change behaviour and flow of execution based on whether the victim tried to open the devtools of the browser or not.



<span class="line"><!---->I consider this a security issue because this allows attackers detect and change behaviour and flow of execution based on whether the victim tried to open the devtools of the browser or not.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I wrote a lot about this vector of attack which serves the offensive cyber industry quite a lot:



<span class="line"><!---->I wrote a lot about this vector of attack which serves the offensive cyber industry quite a lot:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





* 



<span class="line"><!---->* <!----></span>





https://github.com/weizman/awesome-javascript-anti-debugging



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/weizman/awesome-javascript-anti-debugging"><!---->https://github.com/weizman/awesome-javascript-anti-debugging<!----></a>



<br>





* 



<span class="line"><!---->* <!----></span>





https://weizmangal.com/?tags=Anti-Debug



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://weizmangal.com/?tags=Anti-Debug"><!---->https://weizmangal.com/?tags=Anti-Debug<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





The problem seems to be related to how the devtools are looking up declarative shadow root elements when are asked to output them to the console when they belong to realms (iframes) that were shutdown (detached from dom).



<span class="line"><!---->The problem seems to be related to how the devtools are looking up declarative shadow root elements when are asked to output them to the console when they belong to realms (iframes) that were shutdown (detached from dom).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





Chrome Version: 114.0.0.0 stable



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: 114.0.0.0 stable<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Macintosh; Intel Mac OS X 10_15_7



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Macintosh; Intel Mac OS X 10_15_7<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





Open "poc.html" in chrome (could be served over "file://"). Choose "enable" or "disable" to either enable or disable the poc.



<span class="line"><!---->Open "poc.html" in chrome (could be served over "file://"). Choose "enable" or "disable" to either enable or disable the poc.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





FOR CRASHES, PLEASE INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING ADDITIONAL INFORMATION



<b class="line"><!---->FOR CRASHES, PLEASE INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING ADDITIONAL INFORMATION<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





Type of crash: tab + devtools



<span class="line"><!---->Type of crash: tab + devtools<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

Thanks for the report. I was able to reproduce on Windows Extended Stable (114). 



<span class="line"><!---->Thanks for the report. I was able to reproduce on Windows Extended Stable (114). <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is definitely a bug, but despite the error I'm having an oddly hard time exposing more details about the crash, such as which process is dying. This is open to revision as we understand the bug better, but I'm tentatively categorizing this report as Medium severity under the conservative assumption that it's memory corruption due to the STATUS_ACCESS_VIOLATION message in the sad tab page that's occurring within a sandboxed process because the whole browser would presumably come down if the crash occurred in the browser process, and downgrading severity from High to Medium because triggering the bug requires the user to open DevTools.



<span class="line"><!---->This is definitely a bug, but despite the error I'm having an oddly hard time exposing more details about the crash, such as which process is dying. This is open to revision as we understand the bug better, but I'm tentatively categorizing this report as Medium severity under the conservative assumption that it's memory corruption due to the STATUS_ACCESS_VIOLATION message in the sad tab page that's occurring within a sandboxed process because the whole browser would presumably come down if the crash occurred in the browser process, and downgrading severity from High to Medium because triggering the bug requires the user to open DevTools.<!----></span>

Thank you for this report. In reviewing this issue, this appears that it would simply result in a null ptr deref and is not exploitable / resulting in security consequences to a user. In lieu of further information to demonstrate security implications resulting from this crash, I'm going to convert this issue to type=bug and consider it to not be eligible for a VRP reward.

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM

        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;

          position: absolute;
